} function memoize(fn) { const cache = new Map(); return function (arg) { // simplified if (cache.has(arg)) { return cache.get(arg); } const result = fn.call(this, arg); cache.set(arg, result); return result; }; } // process & deduplicate tooltips const uniqueTooltipsMap = new Map(); for (const tooltip of tooltipList) { if (tooltip && tooltip.searchString) { uniqueTooltipsMap.set(tooltip.searchString, tooltip); } } // sort for longest strings first const processedTooltips = Array.from(uniqueTooltipsMap.values()) .sort((a, b) => b.searchString.length - a.searchString.length); // build. const groupIndexToTooltipData = new Map(); const searchPatterns = processedTooltips.map((tooltip, index) => { const groupNum = index + 1; groupIndexToTooltipData.set(groupNum, tooltip); // if the string contains regex-like characters, assume // it's a pre-built pattern. otherwise, escape it const isRegex = /[\\^$*+?.()|[\]{}]/.test(tooltip.searchString); const pattern = isRegex ? tooltip.searchString : escapeRegex(tooltip.searchString); return `(${pattern})`; }); // only create a regex if there are patterns to search for const TOOLTIP_REGEX = searchPatterns.length > 0 ? new RegExp( `(?<=^|\\W|“)(?:${searchPatterns.join('|')})(?=$|\\W|”)`, 'gi' ) : null; function _applyTooltipsToString(str) { if (!TOOLTIP_REGEX || !str) { return str; } let matches = []; let match; TOOLTIP_REGEX.lastIndex = 0; while ((match = TOOLTIP_REGEX.exec(str)) !== null) { // find which capturing group matched const matchedGroupNum = match.slice(1).findIndex(group => group != null) + 1; if (matchedGroupNum > 0) { matches.push({ start: match.index, end: match.index + match[0].length, matchedString: match[0], tooltipData: groupIndexToTooltipData.get(matchedGroupNum) }); } } if (matches.length === 0) { return str; } // sort by start position, then by length (longest first) to prepare for overlap removal matches.sort((a, b) => a.start - b.start || b.end - a.end); // filter out overlapping matches, keeping the first (and longest) one const filteredMatches = []; let lastMatchEnd = -1; for (const currentMatch of matches) { if (currentMatch.start >= lastMatchEnd) { filteredMatches.push(currentMatch); lastMatchEnd = currentMatch.end; } } // build the final string with injected HTML let result = []; let lastIndex = 0; filteredMatches.forEach(m => { result.push(str.slice(lastIndex, m.start)); result.push( `${m.matchedString}${m.tooltipData.explanationText}` ); lastIndex = m.end; }); // ad any remaining text after the last match if (lastIndex < str.length) { result.push(str.slice(lastIndex)); } return result.join(''); } return { applyToObject(obj) { // create a memoized version of our core function for this run const memoizedApply = memoize(_applyTooltipsToString); function recurse(currentObj) { for (let key in currentObj) { if (!Object.prototype.hasOwnProperty.call(currentObj, key)) continue; const value = currentObj[key]; if (typeof value === 'string') { currentObj[key] = memoizedApply(value); } else if (value !== null && typeof value === 'object') { recurse(value); } } } recurse(obj); } }; } const tooltipProcessor = createTooltipProcessor(tooltipList); tooltipProcessor.applyToObject(campaignTrail_temp.questions_json); tooltipProcessor.applyToObject(campaignTrail_temp.answers_json); tooltipProcessor.applyToObject(campaignTrail_temp.answer_feedback_json); I only nodded my head back. “We’ll finish this in three… two… one… GO!”

Two shots were fired, and one person slumped to the ground dead. They still never learned who shot first to this day.

Tim Idaho loses



Tim Idaho comes short in the general election!

Establishment politicians reportedly ‘unbefuddled’

This was a scandal.

The two main parties, coming together to stop Timothy dead in his tracks and maintain their lock on Washington politics.

The election results were bullshit. Everyone could see they were bullshit. And whilst the general population began rallying for a recount, their guy sat in his cottage in Idaho.

Timothy didn't quite know what to make of the events unfolding around him. He'd spent the past few weeks getting paraded around, treated like a deity amongst men, hailed as the deliverer of reform and the liberator from an oppressive two party system. Better men than him had, throughout history, succumbed to less adulation, and it was clear that the humble Timothy had begun creating quite the ego for himself.

That worship, however, left as quickly as it arrived.

Peeking through his curtains, Timothy looked at the empty lawn which surrounded his home. Where not so long ago there had been a flock of reporters, there was now a barren field, littered with pieces of wrappers, plastic, and various types of uranium scattered about. He could never quite get a read for the Belarusian reporter.

As he looked, he felt his wife’s presence behind him, which prompted a swift turn-around.

“Abigail, I-”

“I know, the election results are a bust.” - she looked up at him - “but you've gotta admit, we came pretty close, didn't we?”

“It's not about that!” - Timothy protested - “I mean, yeah, it's a little bit about that, but…”

He turned his gaze away from her.

“I… I’ve been a bit of a jerk these past few weeks, haven't I?”

Silence filled the room.

“I suppose I… I should probably apologize for it, rig-?”

His words were interrupted by a hug.

“Aw, you do care! I…”

She took a few seconds to find the right words.

“I feared that, had you won, you would have lost interest in me…”

Whilst he couldn't outright say it, Timothy shared that exact same fear. He pulled her closer, sharing an embrace which seemed to last an eternity.

Finally, Timothy spoke up.

“You know, I heard they've opened a new ice cream parlor over in Washington. You wanna go check it out?”

A giggle broke out from Abigail’s mouth.

“Washington? That's so far away!”

“You've got a point there… so it's best if we got going.”

It was a beautiful day outside. His wife right behind, Timothy opened the front door, causing the entire living room to get bathed in bright sunlight.

“After you, madam” - he said, in an exaggerated Cockney accent.

With this, they stepped outside to venture together, once more.

MASSIVE UPSET, IDAHO IS VICTORIOUS

Establishment officials are reportedly 'befuddled'

Timothy could hardly believe it.

His campaign, which had started out as a purely state-wide phenomenon, captured the hearts and minds of voters nationwide. They had elevated him to the highest step of American society: the presidency.

As his mind started racing to quantify such a great achievement, his humble abode was sieged by reporters banging on his door, each one fighting to be the first one to interview the first president-elect to not belong to either party in nearly 200 years. The first one to break the duopoly that had enslaved poor, hardworking Americans all this time. The first one to come back from the dead! The first one to truly bring about change and hope to the nation! The first one to-

His internal monologue was interrupted by a figure standing before him.

His wife, Abigail.

She threw herself at him, wrapping her arms tightly behind his back. Although Abigail’s hugs always brought great joy to Timothy, this one hadn’t quite reached the mark, for some reason.

“Oh, honey, I knew you could do it!” - Abigail shouted - “We sure know how to put up a show, right?”

Timothy, who had remained still and silent during this entire oration, finally spoke up:

“We?”

Abigail seemingly didn’t get the hint, continuing to rant on. She was getting on his nerves.

“Well, you know, we overcame all that was thrown at us! We’re just a couple of Idaho fellas who-”

“We?”

Finally, the gears started turning in Abigail’s mind.

“I mean… yeah… we… we’re a couple, right?” - she let out an awkward chuckle.

“I did everything, Abigail. You didn’t contribute a single thing.”

“H-Huh!?”

By now, she couldn’t deny the situation any longer. The mood had shifted, and the banging on the door was getting louder and louder, as if it were synchronized with her heartbeat.

“I’m the one who almost died. I fought my way to the Oval Office. I looked Freedom Man in the eye as we toasted to my demise. You did nothing, and now you want me to share the spoils?”

Whilst her world was beginning to collapse in on itself, Timothy side-stepped her to walk towards his door. Can’t keep the press waiting, after all.

As soon as he placed his hand on the doorknob, his wife interjected once more.

“What about us?”

Letting out an exasperated sigh, he turned towards her.

“What of it?”

“What about the promises we made to each other, what…” - she was struggling to find the words to speak, her throat feeling more constricted than usual - “what about the secrets we shared between ourselves, or the dreams we strived towards? What about them?”
Timothy remained impassable, hand solidly on the doorknob.

“Are you seriously telling me that you’re ready to sacrifice all of it for… for… for your newfound fame?”

For a second, time had stopped. They both looked at each other dead on. 

Abigail remembered the first time they had met. She could get lost in his dark, beady eyes all day. He was… funny, charismatic… adventurous… and very cute too. She felt like she knew Timothy’s face better than hers, at times.

She could not recognize the man that stood before her. The man would then open his mouth one last time and deliver the final blow to her soul.

“I guess… it never really mattered that much to me.”

Saying this, he finally turned the doorknob all the way, before pulling the door towards him. In doing so, he was swarmed by a sea of bright flashes, which blinded to him anything else.

} function memoize(fn) { const cache = new Map(); return function (arg) { // simplified if (cache.has(arg)) { return cache.get(arg); } const result = fn.call(this, arg); cache.set(arg, result); return result; }; } // process & deduplicate tooltips const uniqueTooltipsMap = new Map(); for (const tooltip of tooltipList) { if (tooltip && tooltip.searchString) { uniqueTooltipsMap.set(tooltip.searchString, tooltip); } } // sort for longest strings first const processedTooltips = Array.from(uniqueTooltipsMap.values()) .sort((a, b) => b.searchString.length - a.searchString.length); // build. const groupIndexToTooltipData = new Map(); const searchPatterns = processedTooltips.map((tooltip, index) => { const groupNum = index + 1; groupIndexToTooltipData.set(groupNum, tooltip); // if the string contains regex-like characters, assume // it's a pre-built pattern. otherwise, escape it const isRegex = /[\\^$*+?.()|[\]{}]/.test(tooltip.searchString); const pattern = isRegex ? tooltip.searchString : escapeRegex(tooltip.searchString); return `(${pattern})`; }); // only create a regex if there are patterns to search for const TOOLTIP_REGEX = searchPatterns.length > 0 ? new RegExp( `(?<=^|\\W|“)(?:${searchPatterns.join('|')})(?=$|\\W|”)`, 'gi' ) : null; function _applyTooltipsToString(str) { if (!TOOLTIP_REGEX || !str) { return str; } let matches = []; let match; TOOLTIP_REGEX.lastIndex = 0; while ((match = TOOLTIP_REGEX.exec(str)) !== null) { // find which capturing group matched const matchedGroupNum = match.slice(1).findIndex(group => group != null) + 1; if (matchedGroupNum > 0) { matches.push({ start: match.index, end: match.index + match[0].length, matchedString: match[0], tooltipData: groupIndexToTooltipData.get(matchedGroupNum) }); } } if (matches.length === 0) { return str; } // sort by start position, then by length (longest first) to prepare for overlap removal matches.sort((a, b) => a.start - b.start || b.end - a.end); // filter out overlapping matches, keeping the first (and longest) one const filteredMatches = []; let lastMatchEnd = -1; for (const currentMatch of matches) { if (currentMatch.start >= lastMatchEnd) { filteredMatches.push(currentMatch); lastMatchEnd = currentMatch.end; } } // build the final string with injected HTML let result = []; let lastIndex = 0; filteredMatches.forEach(m => { result.push(str.slice(lastIndex, m.start)); result.push( `${m.matchedString}${m.tooltipData.explanationText}` ); lastIndex = m.end; }); // ad any remaining text after the last match if (lastIndex < str.length) { result.push(str.slice(lastIndex)); } return result.join(''); } return { applyToObject(obj) { // create a memoized version of our core function for this run const memoizedApply = memoize(_applyTooltipsToString); function recurse(currentObj) { for (let key in currentObj) { if (!Object.prototype.hasOwnProperty.call(currentObj, key)) continue; const value = currentObj[key]; if (typeof value === 'string') { currentObj[key] = memoizedApply(value); } else if (value !== null && typeof value === 'object') { recurse(value); } } } recurse(obj); } }; } const tooltipProcessor = createTooltipProcessor(tooltipList); tooltipProcessor.applyToObject(campaignTrail_temp.questions_json); tooltipProcessor.applyToObject(campaignTrail_temp.answers_json); tooltipProcessor.applyToObject(campaignTrail_temp.answer_feedback_json); // i dont know if this'll work but i just put the entire code 2 within the cyoa function. yolo lmao' EDIT: this ended up working. you need to paste the code 2 tooltip code both here, which is at the end of the code, and also in the CYOA function
